<p>The <b>June 2012 Greek legislative election</b> was held in <a href="/wiki/Greece" title="Greece">Greece</a> on Sunday, 17 June,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup> to elect all 300 members to the <a href="/wiki/Hellenic_Parliament" title="Hellenic Parliament">Hellenic Parliament</a> in accordance with the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Greece" title="Constitution of Greece">constitution</a>, after all <a href="/wiki/Greek_government_formation,_May_2012" title="Greek government formation, May 2012">attempts to form a new government</a> failed following the <a href="/wiki/Greek_legislative_election,_May_2012" title="Greek legislative election, May 2012">May election</a>. If all attempts to form a new government fails, the constitution directs the <a href="/wiki/President_of_Greece" title="President of Greece">president</a> to dissolve a newly elected parliament, and then to call for new parliamentary elections within 30 days of the dissolution. The president announced at 16 May the date for the new election, and signed the formal decrete to dissolve the parliament and call for the election at 19 May.</p>
<p>The election result featured <a href="/wiki/New_Democracy_(Greece)" title="New Democracy (Greece)">New Democracy</a> as the largest party, with 30% of the votes and 129 seats (including the 50 extra seats for coming first). The second party was the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Coalition_of_the_Radical_Left" title="Coalition of the Radical Left">Coalition of the Radical Left</a> (SYRIZA) with 27% of the votes and 71 seats. The third party was the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Panhellenic_Socialist_Movement" title="Panhellenic Socialist Movement">Panhellenic Socialist Movement</a> (PASOK) with 12% of the votes and 33 seats. The other parties that won seats were: <a href="/wiki/Independent_Greeks" title="Independent Greeks">Independent Greeks</a> (ANEL) with 20 seats, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Golden_Dawn_(Greece)" title="Golden Dawn (Greece)">Golden Dawn</a> (XA) with 18 seats, <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Left_(Greece)" title="Democratic Left (Greece)">Democratic Left</a> (DIMAR) with 17 seats, and <a href="/wiki/Communist_Party_of_Greece" title="Communist Party of Greece">Communist Party of Greece</a> (KKE) with 12 seats.</p>
<p>None of the parties achieved the 151 seats needed for an overall majority. As outlined by the constitution, the largest party ND led the first negotiations to try and form a new government. ND invited all elected parties, except the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ultranationalist" title="Ultranationalist">ultranationalist</a> party <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Golden_Dawn_(Greece)" title="Golden Dawn (Greece)">Golden Dawn</a> (XA), to participate in a unity government that would respect the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Greek_debt_crisis#Second_rescue_package_.28July_2011_-_February_2012.29" title="Greek debt crisis">existing bailout agreement</a> Greece signed and ratified in February 2012, but as the highest priority should attempt to renegotiate the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Greek_debt_crisis#Fifth_austerity_package_.E2.80.93_February_2012" title="Greek debt crisis">austerity terms of the agreement</a>, asking the main creditors (<a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">EU</a>, <a href="/wiki/European_Central_Bank" title="European Central Bank">ECB</a> and <a href="/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund" title="International Monetary Fund">IMF</a>) to accept milder terms and increase their amount of bailout funding to Greece. On 20 June, a new unity government comprising ND, PASOK and DIMAR was formed for a planned 4-year term, with <a href="/wiki/Antonis_Samaras" title="Antonis Samaras">Antonis Samaras</a> appointed to be the new <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Greece" title="Prime Minister of Greece">Prime Minister</a>. The new cabinet was dominated by lawmakers from ND but also included a significant number of technocrats, among them two ministers (Justice, Administrative Reform) nominated by DIMAR. The other coalition participant, PASOK, opted not to participate with leading party cadres in the government.</p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Background">Background</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Greek_legislative_election,_June_2012&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Background">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>By section 37 of the constitution, the <a href="/wiki/President_of_Greece" title="President of Greece">President of the Republic</a> will consecutively give the leaders of the three largest parties in parliament an exploratory mandate to set up a government within three days, until one leader succeeds. If none does, "the President of the Republic shall summon all party leaders, and if the impossibility to form a Cabinet enjoying the confidence of the Parliament is confirmed, he shall attempt to form a Cabinet composed of all parties in Parliament for the purpose of holding parliamentary elections. If this fails, he shall entrust the President of the Supreme Administrative Court or of the Supreme Civil and Criminal Court or of the Court of Auditors to form a Cabinet as widely accepted as possible to carry out elections and dissolve Parliament."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="May_election">May election</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Greek_legislative_election,_June_2012&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: May election">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Greek_legislative_election,_May_2012" title="Greek legislative election, May 2012">Greek legislative election, May 2012</a></div>
<p>At the 6 May election, no party won an absolute majority of seats. President <a href="/wiki/Karolos_Papoulias" title="Karolos Papoulias">Karolos Papoulias</a>, in accordance with the constitution, offered successive exploratory mandates to the leaders of the three largest parties: <a href="/wiki/Antonis_Samaras" title="Antonis Samaras">Antonis Samaras</a> of <a href="/wiki/New_Democracy_(Greece)" title="New Democracy (Greece)">New Democracy</a> (ND), <a href="/wiki/Alexis_Tsipras" title="Alexis Tsipras">Alexis Tsipras</a> of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Coalition_of_the_Radical_Left" title="Coalition of the Radical Left">Coalition of the Radical Left</a> (SYRIZA), and <a href="/wiki/Evangelos_Venizelos" title="Evangelos Venizelos">Evangelos Venizelos</a> of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Panhellenic_Socialist_Movement" title="Panhellenic Socialist Movement">Panhellenic Socialist Movement</a> (PASOK). Each in turn failed to form a government and returned their mandates to the president.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 13 May, the president followed the terms of section 37 of the constitution and met with all party leaders to find a way of forming a majority government.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup> After concluding on the eve of 14 May that it was impossible to form a new ordinary political government, in a last-ditch effort the president asked all the elected political leaders on 15 May if they could support the establishment of a "technocratic" government for a limited term, to guide Greece safely through its economic crisis. After this attempt also failed,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup> he asked on 16 May, in full compliance with the constitution, for a <a href="/wiki/Caretaker_Cabinet_of_Panagiotis_Pikrammenos" title="Caretaker Cabinet of Panagiotis Pikrammenos">caretaker cabinet</a> under <a href="/wiki/Council_of_State_(Greece)" title="Council of State (Greece)">Council of State</a> president <a href="/wiki/Panagiotis_Pikrammenos" title="Panagiotis Pikrammenos">Panagiotis Pikrammenos</a> to be appointed, and to dissolve parliament and hold new elections on 17 June.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-6">[6]</a></sup> The formal decree to dissolve the newly elected parliament and call for new elections was jointly signed by President Karolos Papoulias and caretaker Prime Minister Panagiotis Pikrammenos at 19 May, to fully comply with the 30-day constitutional rule.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup></p>
<p>German Finance Minister <a href="/wiki/Wolfgang_Sch%C3%A4uble" title="Wolfgang Schäuble">Wolfgang Schäuble</a> said the election would be a referendum on Greece's continuation as a member of the <a href="/wiki/Eurozone" title="Eurozone">eurozone</a>. "If Greece—and this is the will of the great majority—wants to stay in the euro, then they have to accept the conditions," he said. "Otherwise it isn’t possible. No responsible candidate can hide that from the electorate."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bberg_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-bberg-8">[8]</a></sup> Parallels were also drawn to the proposed <a href="/wiki/Greek_proposed_economy_referendum,_2011" title="Greek proposed economy referendum, 2011">Greek economy referendum</a>, with suggestion that the two 2012 elections were a <i>de facto</i> referendum.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Incumbent_parliament">Incumbent parliament</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Greek_legislative_election,_June_2012&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Incumbent parliament">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_members_of_the_Hellenic_Parliament,_May_2012" title="List of members of the Hellenic Parliament, May 2012">List of members of the Hellenic Parliament, May 2012</a></div>
<p>Seven parties were elected at the May 2012 election, but this parliament was short-lived because a coalition government could not be <a href="/wiki/Greek_government_formation,_May_2012" title="Greek government formation, May 2012">formed</a>; fresh elections were called.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Participating_parties">Participating parties</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Greek_legislative_election,_June_2012&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Participating parties">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Parties_declining_to_participate">Parties declining to participate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Greek_legislative_election,_June_2012&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Parties declining to participate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Compared with the <a href="/wiki/Greek_legislative_election,_May_2012#Participating_parties" title="Greek legislative election, May 2012">May 2012 election</a>, and in addition to the unapproved parties above, the following nine parties are not participating in the June 2012 election (in order of the size of their vote in the previous election):</p>
<ol>
<li><a href="/wiki/Democratic_Alliance_(Greece)" title="Democratic Alliance (Greece)">Democratic Alliance</a> (DISY), opting to merge with ND on 22 May.</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Social_Agreement" title="Social Agreement">Social Agreement</a> (KOISY), Louka Katseli</li>
<li>No: The coalition of <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Revival" title="Democratic Revival">Democratic Revival</a> and <a href="/wiki/United_Popular_Front" title="United Popular Front">United Popular Front</a> (EPAM), Stelios Papathemelis and 3-member committee</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/National_Unity_Association" title="National Unity Association">National Unity Association</a> (SEE), N. Alikakos</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Workers_Revolutionary_Party_(Greece)" title="Workers Revolutionary Party (Greece)">Workers Revolutionary Party</a> (EEK), Sabetai Matsas</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Organization_for_the_Reconstruction_of_the_Communist_Party_of_Greece" title="Organization for the Reconstruction of the Communist Party of Greece">Organisation for the Reconstruction of the Communist Party of Greece</a> (OAKKE), 3-member committee</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Organisation_of_Communist_Internationalists_of_Greece" title="Organisation of Communist Internationalists of Greece">Organisation of Communist Internationalists of Greece</a> (OKDE), 3-member committee</li>
<li>Dignity, alliance of independent candidates, Panayiotis Theodoropoulos</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Greek_Ecologists" title="Greek Ecologists">Greek Ecologists</a>, Dimosthenis Vergis</li>
</ol>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Procedure">Procedure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Greek_legislative_election,_June_2012&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Procedure">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Voting is mandatory;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> however none of the legally existing penalties or sanctions have ever been enforced.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> 250 seats will be distributed on the basis of proportional representation, with a threshold of 3% required for entry into parliament. The other 50 seats will be awarded to the party that wins a <a href="/wiki/Plurality_(voting)" title="Plurality (voting)">plurality</a> of votes, with coalitions in that regard not being counted as an overall party but having their votes counted separately for each party in the coalition, according to the <a href="/wiki/Elections_in_Greece#Electoral_law" title="Elections in Greece">election law</a>. Parliamentary majority is achieved by a party or coalition of parties that command at least one half plus one (151 out of 300) of total seats. Blank and invalid votes, as well as votes cast for parties that fall short of the 3% threshold, are disregarded for seat allocation purposes.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Opinion_polls">Opinion polls</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Greek_legislative_election,_June_2012&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Opinion polls">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="center">
<div class="thumb tnone">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:702px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Election_results_and_opinion_polls_in_Greece_(May-June_2012).png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="629" data-file-width="963" height="457" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Election_results_and_opinion_polls_in_Greece_%28May-June_2012%29.png/700px-Election_results_and_opinion_polls_in_Greece_%28May-June_2012%29.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/e/e8/Election_results_and_opinion_polls_in_Greece_%28May-June_2012%29.png 1.5x" width="700"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Election_results_and_opinion_polls_in_Greece_(May-June_2012).png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Opinion polls expressed as an average for each week between the elections at 6 May and 17 June 2012 (based only upon adjusted data)</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Most of the early polls conducted during the 10 days after the election at 6 May—where the political leaders unsuccessfully attempted to form a new government—showed SYRIZA taking the lead in popular support ahead of ND.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> This led to accusations from the political leaders at ND, PASOK and DIMAR, that SYRIZA deliberately had derailed all attempts to form a new government, with the sole purpose of pursuing their own interest of possibly growing in size after a new election.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> After the new June election was officially called at 16 May,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_6-1"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-6">[6]</a></sup> there was an apparent change in political momentum, with most of the subsequent opinion polls now indicating that ND had taken the lead in popular support ahead of SYRIZA. According to Greek law, the polling companies were not allowed to publish additional opinion polls after the last working day two weeks ahead of the election, meaning that the last opinion polls were published at 1 June.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-last_Kapa_poll_conducted_at_29.E2.80.9331_May_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-last_Kapa_poll_conducted_at_29.E2.80.9331_May-20">[20]</a></sup> Among all of the last published opinion polls, 9 out of 12 polling companies measured a lead of popular support for ND, while only the two polling companies, VPRC and Public Issue <small>(who both adjust their vote results by performing a weighted prediction of the likely votes of undecided voters based on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Time_Series_Analysis" title="Time Series Analysis">Time Series Analysis</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-VPRC_opinion_poll_methodology_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-VPRC_opinion_poll_methodology-21">[21]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Public_Issue_opinion_poll_methodology_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-Public_Issue_opinion_poll_methodology-22">[22]</a></sup>)</small> believed the current lead of popular support belonged to SYRIZA, and the last polling company Pulse RC predicted it would end up with a draw.</p>

</table>
<ul>
<li><small><b>Note on varying poll methodology:</b> The polls shown above with figures in yellow lines used the "raw data method", recording raw responses for each party as a percentage of total responses, and including percentages for those who are undecided or said they will abstain to vote (either physically or by voting blank). All the other polls used an "adjusted method" where an estimate of vote share is projected, by disregarding those who opted to abstain and in some manner adjusting for the likely votes of those who were undecided. The adjusted method emulates the same vote percentage calculation as in the official election. The raw data method, will by definition always result in some relative lower percentage points for all parties (due to the party votes now being divided by the higher figure "total of all responses", instead of divided by the lower figure "total of all valid votes"). Therefore, the percentage numbers listed by each of these two methods are not directly comparable to each other. For some polls, the data from both methods are presented.</small></li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Secret_polling">Secret polling</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Greek_legislative_election,_June_2012&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Secret polling">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>According to Greek law, opinion polls are not allowed to be published after the last working day two weeks ahead of the official election day, and as a result the last date to publish a poll was 1 June 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-last_Kapa_poll_conducted_at_29.E2.80.9331_May_20-2"><a href="#cite_note-last_Kapa_poll_conducted_at_29.E2.80.9331_May-20">[20]</a></sup> However, the polling companies are still allowed to conduct opinion polls during the last two weeks of the election campaign for research purpose, as long as the results remain unpublished and secret. Greek banking stocks were up 20% on Thursday 15 June 2012, on reports that a secret poll had indicated that a pro-bailout government was likely to emerge.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup></p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Exit_polls">Exit polls</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Greek_legislative_election,_June_2012&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Exit polls">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The first exit polls, being based upon 80% of the interviewed voters and published at 7pm, had New Democracy narrowly in the lead, far within the margin of error.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-First_exit_poll_64-0"><a href="#cite_note-First_exit_poll-64">[64]</a></sup> While the second exit poll, being based upon 100% of the interviewed voters and published at 8pm, now had New Democracy with a clear lead over Syriza, exceeding the margin of error.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Second_exit_poll_65-0"><a href="#cite_note-Second_exit_poll-65">[65]</a></sup></p>
<table class="wikitable unsortable">
<tr>

<th><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Coalition_of_the_Radical_Left" title="Coalition of the Radical Left">SYRIZA</a></th>

<p>According to the analysis of exit poll, SYRIZA had a significant lead for the age groups 18–34 years and 35–54 years, while ND had a significant lead in regards of the age group above 55 years:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Exit_polls_for_age_groups_67-0"><a href="#cite_note-Exit_polls_for_age_groups-67">[67]</a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li>Exit poll (18–34 years): <b>SYRIZA=33%</b>, ND=20%, PASOK=6%.</li>
<li>Exit poll (35–54 years): <b>SYRIZA=34%</b>, ND=24%, PASOK=8%.</li>
<li>Exit poll (&gt; 55 years): SYRIZA=20%, <b>ND=39%</b>, PASOK=17%.</li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Campaign">Campaign</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Greek_legislative_election,_June_2012&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Campaign">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Even before the election had been called, <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Left_(Greece)" title="Democratic Left (Greece)">Democratic Left</a> (DIMAR) leader Kouvelis stated that DIMAR would likely not want to participate in a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Coalition_of_the_Radical_Left" title="Coalition of the Radical Left">Coalition of the Radical Left</a> (SYRIZA) led government even after repeated elections, as SYRIZA had declined to participate in a unity government with <a href="/wiki/New_Democracy_(Greece)" title="New Democracy (Greece)">New Democracy</a> (ND), <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Panhellenic_Socialist_Movement" title="Panhellenic Socialist Movement">Panhellenic Socialist Movement</a> (PASOK), and DIMAR.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup></p>
<p>Before the election, it was expected that larger parties would try to form alliances with smaller parties; specifically, ND was in negotiations with <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Alliance_(Greece)" title="Democratic Alliance (Greece)">Democratic Alliance</a> (DISY), while DISY was also negotiating with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Drasi" title="Drasi">Action</a> (DRASI),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup> and SYRIZA was trying to form an alliance with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Social_Agreement" title="Social Agreement">Social Agreement</a> (KOISY).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> There were also rumours of SYRIZA negotiating with the <a href="/wiki/Ecologist_Greens" title="Ecologist Greens">Ecologist Greens</a> (OP) and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Front_of_the_Greek_Anticapitalist_Left" title="Front of the Greek Anticapitalist Left">Anticapitalist Left Cooperation for the Overthrow -Front of anticapitalist, revolutionary, communist and radical Left Ecology</a> (ANTARSYA).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> The other left parties however all ended to decide they would not merge or form a new coalition with SYRIZA. Another important change however happened for SYRIZA on 22 May, where the steering committee decided to transform the "Coalition of the Radical Left", from its 10 coalition parties into a single independent party with the new name "Syriza Unionist Social Front".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup> The driving force behind the transformation from coalition to a united party, was the current Greek election law, stipulating that any coalitions participating in a parliamentary election should have their votes split up for each party in the coalition, before determining who became the largest party in the election and thus qualified to win the 50 extra bonus seats in the parliament. So the transformation by itself, greatly increased the chance of SYRIZA also to win bonus seats in the election.</p>
<p>ND and DISY announced a complete merger of the two parties into an overall united party on 21 May,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup> and the following three parties announced on the same day an agreement to run the election as a new joint coalition: <a href="/wiki/Recreate_Greece" title="Recreate Greece">Recreate Greece</a> – <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Drasi" title="Drasi">Action</a> – <a href="/wiki/Liberal_Alliance_(Greece)" title="Liberal Alliance (Greece)">Liberal Alliance</a> (DX-DRASI-FS).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup></p>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Social_Agreement" title="Social Agreement">Social Agreement</a> announced at 19 May their main goal was to establish a new "left government", and in order to achieve such a goal, they would abstain to participate in the election, and instead use all their energy to arrange meetings with all other progressive left parties, with the purpose of creating a convergence program for the parties to make formation of a new "left government" possible after the elections in June.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup> On 28 May the <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Left_(Greece)" title="Democratic Left (Greece)">Democratic Left</a> (DIMAR) however repeated their previous stance, that it would only work with SYRIZA to form a "left government", on the condition that there were guarantees of staying within the eurozone, and this would according to DIMAR require SYRIZA to drop their idea of a unilateral cancellation of the "memorandum" (a nickname for: "The bailout deal that the previous Greek government agreed to implement with EU, <a href="/wiki/European_Central_Bank" title="European Central Bank">ECB</a> and <a href="/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund" title="International Monetary Fund">IMF</a>").<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup> As none of the other left parties (OP, ANTARSYA and KKE), neither wanted to accept signing the proposed agreement of a unilateral rejection of the "memorandum" in favour of SYRIZAs new "National Recovery Plan", the attempt by Social Agreement to form a multilateral agreement between "all progressive left parties" ahead of the election failed. Instead only a small bilateral agreement between SYRIZA and Social Agreement was signed, outlining what the cornerstones of the new policy should be, if the election ended with a parliamentary majority for SYRIZA to form a one party government.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup> On 7 June, the executive committee of Social Agreement decided they did not want to merge with SYRIZA, and reaffirmed they neither wanted to participate in any political coalitions, because they believed it was needed for them to stay as an independent neutral party, in order best to help creating a consensus among the left parties to form a new SYRIZA led government.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 7 June, an arrest warrant was issued for <a href="/wiki/Ilias_Kasidiaris" title="Ilias Kasidiaris">Ilias Kasidiaris</a> from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Golden_Dawn_(Greece)" title="Golden Dawn (Greece)">Golden Dawn</a> (XA), after he during a political debate broadcast by ANT-1 TV, as reported by the newspaper Kathimerini: "threw water at SYRIZA’s <a href="/wiki/Rena_Dourou" title="Rena Dourou">Rena Dourou</a> and then repeatedly slapped Communist Party hopeful <a href="/wiki/Liana_Kanelli" title="Liana Kanelli">Liana Kanelli</a>", before the televised signal was interrupted.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Arrest_warrant_for_Kasidiaris_82-0"><a href="#cite_note-Arrest_warrant_for_Kasidiaris-82">[82]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Video_clip_of_Kasidiaris_punching_83-0"><a href="#cite_note-Video_clip_of_Kasidiaris_punching-83">[83]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Caretaker_government" title="Caretaker government">caretaker government</a> and all parties, except for the leader of Golden Dawn, jointly condemned the TV show attack by Kasidiaris with the following statements:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Government_and_all_parties_condemn_Golden_Dawn_84-0"><a href="#cite_note-Government_and_all_parties_condemn_Golden_Dawn-84">[84]</a></sup> The spokesman<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Words_to_watch#Unsupported_attributions" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Words to watch"><span title="The material near this tag possibly uses too-vague attribution or weasel words. (June 2012)">who?</span></a></i>]</sup> from the caretaker government <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Dimitris_Tsiodras&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Dimitris Tsiodras (page does not exist)">Dimitris Tsiodras</a> said: "This attack is an attack against every democratic citizen. The least that any democratic citizen could expect is for Mr Kasidiaris’s party, Golden Dawn, to condemn these actions unreservedly." ND, PASOK, SYRIZA and <a href="/wiki/Independent_Greeks" title="Independent Greeks">ANEL</a> also jointly agreed, not to take part in any television or radio panel discussions with Golden Dawn candidates.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> An opinion poll published at 1 June by GPO, had indicated that 60% of the votes received by Golden Dawn in the May election, came from Greeks who wanted to express their opposition to the political establishment, while less than 30% of those voting for the party actually supported its extreme views on immigration. A spokesperson from PASOK said: "This young man proved today that he represents a neo-Nazi group, which apart from being far-right is also cowardly and thuggish" and called for those who previously voted for the party to "think again" before casting their June vote. ANEL leader <a href="/wiki/Panos_Kammenos" title="Panos Kammenos">Panos Kammenos</a> launched the same message by saying "the neo-Nazis have been unmasked on TV. People who voted for the Nazi thugs should react when casting their vote next time."<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> <a href="/wiki/Popular_Orthodox_Rally" title="Popular Orthodox Rally">LAOS</a>' <a href="/wiki/Georgios_Karatzaferis" title="Georgios Karatzaferis">Georgios Karatzaferis</a>, said Golden Dawn was damaging the country's patriotic front: "It took us 10 years to gain respect and dignity for the patriotic movement. We won't let the party of <a href="/wiki/Nikolaos_Michaloliakos" title="Nikolaos Michaloliakos">Nikolaos Michaloliakos</a> and the parliamentary gang of Mr Kasidiaris to ridicule what we have built all these years. It is time for them to leave political life. Fascism will not pass in Greece."<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>During the campaign, the 8 largest parties presented some political ultimatums about a possible government formation after the election:</p>
<table class="wikitable" style="text-align:left;">
<tr>
<th>Party name</th>
<th>Ultimatums to participate in a new government formation</th>
</tr>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="EU_influence">EU influence</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Greek_legislative_election,_June_2012&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: EU influence">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Few hours after the public announcement of the failed attempt by the Greek president to form a new government on 15 May, some Greek officials claimed that German Chancellor <a href="/wiki/Angela_Merkel" title="Angela Merkel">Angela Merkel</a> had suggested to the Greek president during a telephone call, that he should consider to launch a "euro referendum" along with the new "legislative election".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_89-0"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-89">[89]</a></sup> The Greek media and the heads of ND, PASOK, SYRIZA, KKE, and the interim prime minister, all went out strongly to criticise that Merkel purportedly had made such advice.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup> One day later it became clear the entire debate had been based on a translated misunderstanding, as Merkel officially denied ever to have made such a proposition to the Greek president. Merkel insisted that she said the election was "in principle...an indirect referendum on euro membership", as the outcome of the election potentially could lead to a development with Greece leaving the euro, if the election was won by parties supporting a Greek rejection of all commitments signed in the Memorandum.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup> British Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/David_Cameron" title="David Cameron">David Cameron</a>, representing a neutral nation outside the euro, a few days later completely agreed with Merkel's analysis, that the Greek legislative election in principle was "an indirect referendum on euro membership".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup></p>
<p>An EU summit ended on 24 May with repeated calls for Greece to stick to the terms of the EU/IMF memorandum, if they wanted to receive more funds to tackle its debt problem and current economic crisis.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_89-1"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-89">[89]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the wake of the discussions, SYRIZA's leader Tsipras visited some of the main European cities,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup> to clarify his stance of wishing to unilaterally cancel the Memorandum and at the same time having Greece stay within the eurozone.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup> When the French Finance Minister <a href="/wiki/Pierre_Moscovici" title="Pierre Moscovici">Pierre Moscovici</a> on 5 June repeated the European message that a continued euro membership was conditional on the next Greek government continuing to respect the signed commitments in the Memorandum, as the EU would only be willing to accept a re-negotiation of some subterms, Tsipras claimed this was political bluffing and a new message compared to what the French government previously had told him.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Results">Results</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Greek_legislative_election,_June_2012&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Results">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<p>Due to unforeseen circumstances,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (June 2012)">clarification needed</span></a></i>]</sup> voting at the 18th polling station of the Athens A' Electoral District was aborted. In accordance with Article 102 of the electoral law, a new election will be held on 24 June and the 539 registered voters will be asked to cast their ballot again.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Reactions">Reactions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Greek_legislative_election,_June_2012&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Reactions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hellenic_Parliament_Structure_June_2012_visualizing_%2B50_bonus.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="185" data-file-width="360" height="180" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Hellenic_Parliament_Structure_June_2012_visualizing_%2B50_bonus.svg/350px-Hellenic_Parliament_Structure_June_2012_visualizing_%2B50_bonus.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Hellenic_Parliament_Structure_June_2012_visualizing_%2B50_bonus.svg/525px-Hellenic_Parliament_Structure_June_2012_visualizing_%2B50_bonus.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Hellenic_Parliament_Structure_June_2012_visualizing_%2B50_bonus.svg/700px-Hellenic_Parliament_Structure_June_2012_visualizing_%2B50_bonus.svg.png 2x" width="350"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hellenic_Parliament_Structure_June_2012_visualizing_%2B50_bonus.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Seats won in the new parliament
<div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:blue; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;"> </span> <a href="/wiki/New_Democracy_(Greece)" title="New Democracy (Greece)">New Democracy</a>: 79 seats</div>
<div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #C0C0C0; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;"> </span>  &gt; bonus 50 seats to the leading party, ND</div>
<div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #ff8080; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;"> </span> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Coalition_of_the_Radical_Left" title="Coalition of the Radical Left">Syriza Unionist Social Front</a>: 71 seats</div>
<div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:green; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;"> </span> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Panhellenic_Socialist_Movement" title="Panhellenic Socialist Movement">Panhellenic Socialist Movement</a>: 33 seats</div>
<div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:aqua; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;"> </span> <a href="/wiki/Independent_Greeks" title="Independent Greeks">Independent Greeks</a>: 20 seats</div>
<div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #00022D; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;"> </span> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Golden_Dawn_(Greece)" title="Golden Dawn (Greece)">Golden Dawn</a>: 18 seats</div>
<div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:orangered; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;"> </span> <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Left_(Greece)" title="Democratic Left (Greece)">Democratic Left</a>: 17 seats</div>
<div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:red; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;"> </span> <a href="/wiki/Communist_Party_of_Greece" title="Communist Party of Greece">Communist Party</a>: 12 seats</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Eurozone" title="Eurozone">Eurozone</a> finance ministers were quick to issue a statement that read the result "should allow for the formation of a government that will carry the support of the electorate to bring Greece back on a path of sustainable growth...The Eurogroup reiterates its commitment to assist Greece in its adjustment effort in order to address the many challenges the economy is facing." It also said the "troika" of the European Commission, European Central Bank and International Monetary Fund would re-visit Athens to continue discussions on the bailout agreement.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup> On his way to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2012_G-20_Mexico_summit" title="2012 G-20 Mexico summit">2012 G-20 Mexico summit</a>, British Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/David_Cameron" title="David Cameron">David Cameron</a> warned of delayed government formation and said that "the outcome of the Greek election looks clear in terms of a commitment to stay in the eurozone and to accept the terms of the memorandum. But I think those parties that want that to happen can't afford to delay and position themselves. If you are a Greek political party and want to stay in the eurozone and accept the consequences that follow you have got to get on with it and help form a government. A delay could be very dangerous."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tele_101-0"><a href="#cite_note-tele-101">[101]</a></sup> European Union President <a href="/wiki/Herman_Van_Rompuy" title="Herman Van Rompuy">Herman Van Rompuy</a> issued a statement that read: "We will continue to stand by Greece."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bloom_102-0"><a href="#cite_note-bloom-102">[102]</a></sup> He added that "we are confident that the new government will take ownership of the adjustment program to which the Greek authorities had committed earlier this year." <a href="/wiki/European_Commission" title="European Commission">European Commission</a> President <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jose_Manuel_Barroso" title="Jose Manuel Barroso">Jose Manuel Barroso</a> reiterated a willingness to visit Greece when a new government is formed to keep the country on track to continue receiving the bailout money.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup></p>
<p>New Democracy's Antonis Samaras said that "there’s no time to lose or leeway for small party games. The country must be governed." PASOK's Evangelos Venizelos said that "there's not even a day to lose" in the need to form a new government.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bloom_102-1"><a href="#cite_note-bloom-102">[102]</a></sup> Samaras also said the election was a mandate to stay within the eurozone.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup> Golden Dawn's <a href="/wiki/Nikolaos_Michaloliakos" title="Nikolaos Michaloliakos">Nikolaos Michaloliakos</a> said that he "would like to thank the hundreds of thousands of Greeks who did not change their vote, despite the effort of wretched propaganda by the paid stooges on TV. We will continue the fight for a Greece that belongs to Greeks." In <a href="/wiki/Thessaloniki" title="Thessaloniki">Thessaloniki</a>, Golden Dawn's supporters celebrated the result and set off flares and fireworks.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hpost_105-0"><a href="#cite_note-hpost-105">[105]</a></sup></p>
<p>The following day, <a href="/wiki/Financial_market" title="Financial market">financial markets</a> initially rose on the news of ND's plurality, but later came down as the possible implications became known.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tele_101-1"><a href="#cite_note-tele-101">[101]</a></sup> On 19 June, European and American financial markets rose on speculation of the imminence of a new government that would have at least a modicum of support for the bailout programme.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Analysis">Analysis</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Greek_legislative_election,_June_2012&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Analysis">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Huffington_Post" title="Huffington Post">Huffington Post</a></i> read Golden Dawn's popularity as a "symptom of the alienation and hardship that their society is experiencing."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hpost_105-1"><a href="#cite_note-hpost-105">[105]</a></sup> The statement was echoed by <i><a href="/wiki/Fox_News" title="Fox News">Fox News</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup> The <i><a href="/wiki/BBC" title="BBC">BBC</a></i> cited Greece's <a href="/wiki/Debt-to-GDP_ratio" title="Debt-to-GDP ratio">debt-to-GDP ratio</a> and forecasts to ask if an exit from the eurozone was only delayed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Al_Jazeera" title="Al Jazeera">Al Jazeera</a></i> said the May election was a vote out of anger over the austerity measures, but that this was a vote out of fear after the in terms of a more defined future. It cited Samaras' question of staying within the eurozone or returning to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Drachma" title="Drachma">drachma</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup> It also asked if a "Grexit" (Greek exit) from the eurozone was inevitable and cited this as Europe's "Lehman moment" in reference to the <a href="/wiki/Bankruptcy_of_Lehman_Brothers" title="Bankruptcy of Lehman Brothers">bankruptcy of Lehman Brothers</a>. It further cited the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Bank_of_Scotland" title="Royal Bank of Scotland">Royal Bank of Scotland</a>'s assertion that there was a 90 percent chance of a Greek exit from the eurozone within 12–18 months, while <a href="/wiki/Citigroup" title="Citigroup">Citigroup</a> estimated a 50-75 percent chance of an exit. <a href="/wiki/UBS" title="UBS">UBS</a> suggested a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Write_off" title="Write off">write off</a> of 60 billion euros of Greece's debts, as opposed to a between 225 billion to 800 billion euros if Greece were to leave the eurozone. Greece was already expected to be unable to pay pensions and civil servant salaries by mid-July should there be no more external funds coming into the country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Foreign_Affairs" title="Foreign Affairs">Foreign Affairs</a></i> suggested that the election determined whether Greece would exit the eurozone and decide the fate of the entire postwar European project.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government_formation">Government formation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Greek_legislative_election,_June_2012&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Government formation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Cabinet_of_Antonis_Samaras" title="Cabinet of Antonis Samaras">Cabinet of Antonis Samaras</a></div>
<p>New Democracy announced it was working towards building a "pro-euro" coalition.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup> The next day Samaras was tasked with forming a new government within the stipulated three days.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup> SYRIZA announced that it would not join a coalition government which would include a party that insists on going ahead with the austerity measures demanded by the "troika." However, PASOK's Evangelos Venizelos met with Samaras and then announced that "the most crucial thing for us right now is to achieve the greatest possible range of consensus, and this must happen by [19 June] at the latest;" he then went on to criticise Tsipras' refusal to join the government in saying that "you can't have some people choosing the easy position of being in opposition and lying in wait for the government to fail - or rather trying to create the conditions for the government, that is the country, to fail."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aljazeera1_115-0"><a href="#cite_note-aljazeera1-115">[115]</a></sup> On 19 June, ND suggested it was on the verge of forming a coalition government with PASOK and DIMAR, though the latter's Fotis Kouvelis said that he would only offer conditional support. The same morning Samaras met with Kouvelis to gauge support for a three-party coalition. <i><a href="/wiki/Ta_Nea" title="Ta Nea">Ta Nea</a></i> exclaimed in an <a href="/wiki/Op-ed" title="Op-ed">op-ed</a> that "political leaders should be aware of the fact that this government is Greece's last chance to remain in the eurozone. The Greek people are ready to reward the parties that manage to ease austerity and punish those that raise voices of dissent."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup> ND then claimed to have a preliminary agreement with PASOK in order to form a <a href="/wiki/National_unity_government" title="National unity government">government of national salvation</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aljazeera1_115-1"><a href="#cite_note-aljazeera1-115">[115]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 20 June, ND announced a coalition government with PASOK and DIMAR after resuming talks for a common policy programme. Greek media speculated on who would be in the cabinet, including suggestions that the Finance Ministry portfolio would be given to <a href="/wiki/Vassilis_Rapanos" title="Vassilis Rapanos">Vassilis Rapanos</a>, the president of <a href="/wiki/National_Bank_of_Greece" title="National Bank of Greece">National Bank of Greece</a>. PASOK and DIMAR were said to limit their participitation in a new government so as not to be responsible for its actions. They also opposed the inclusion of cabinet members who were previously in the government that approved the bailout programme. Kouvelis said that DIMAR's conditions for joining the coalition government would include an extension of the timetable to meet the target to cut Greece's budget deficit, as well as cutting the <a href="/wiki/Minimum_wage" title="Minimum wage">minimum wage</a> and revoking the austerity measures that had "decimated society."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Greek_legislative_election,_June_2012&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: References">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
